  - Service.

- **File:** `007_Cluster Architecture.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 75 | **Type:** Concept

### Docker-vs-ContainerD

- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 1 | **Type:** Concept
  - So you're going to come across Docker and community many times going forward.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 2 | **Type:** Concept
  - So when you read older blogs or documentation pages, you'll see Docker mentioned along with Kubernetes.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 3 | **Type:** Comparison
  - And when you read newer blogs you will see container D, and you'll wonder what the difference is between the two.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 4 | **Type:** Concept
  - And there are a few CLI tools like Ktor, CRI control or Node Control.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 5 | **Type:** Best Practice
  - And you'll wonder what are these CLI tools and and which one should you be using.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 6 | **Type:** Concept
  - So that's what I'm going to explain in this video.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 7 | **Type:** Concept
  - So let's go back in time to the beginning of the container era.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 8 | **Type:** Concept
  - And in the beginning there was just Docker and there were other tools like rocket.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 9 | **Type:** Concept
  - But Docker's user experience made working with containers super simple, and hence Docker became the most dominant container tool.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 10 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - And then came Kubernetes to orchestrate Docker.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 11 | **Type:** Concept
  - So Kubernetes was built to orchestrate Docker specifically in the beginning.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 12 | **Type:** Concept
  - So Docker and Kubernetes were tightly coupled.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 13 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - And back then Kubernetes only worked with Docker and didn't support any other container solutions.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 14 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - And then Kubernetes grew in popularity as a container orchestrator.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 15 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - And now other container runtimes like rocket wanted in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 16 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - Users needed it to work with container runtimes that are other than just Docker.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 17 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - And so Kubernetes introduced an interface called Container Runtime Interface or Cry.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 18 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So cry allowed any vendor to work as a container runtime for Kubernetes, as long as they adhere to the OCI standards.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 19 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So OCI stands for Open Container Initiative, and it consists of an image spec and a runtime spec.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 20 | **Type:** Best Practice
  - Image spec means the specifications on how, uh, an image should be built.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 21 | **Type:** Concept
  - So that's what I defined.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 22 | **Type:** Best Practice
  - An image spec, defined the specifications on how an image should be built, and the runtime spec defined the standards on how any container runtime should be developed.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 23 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So keeping these standards in mind, anyone can build a container runtime, and that can be used by anybody to to work with Kubernetes.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 24 | **Type:** Concept
  - So that was the idea.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 25 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So rocket and other container runtimes that adhere to the OCI standards were now supported as container runtimes for Kubernetes via the CRI.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 26 | **Type:** Concept
  - However, uh, Docker wasn't built to support the CRI standards because remember, Docker was built way before CRI was introduced and Docker still was the dominant container tool used by most.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 27 | **Type:** Concept
  - Kubernetes had to continue to support Docker as well.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 28 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - And so Kubernetes introduced what is known as uh, Docker shim, which was a hacky, uh, but temporary way to continue to support Docker outside of the container runtime interface.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 29 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So while most other container runtimes worked through the CRI, Docker continued to work without it.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 30 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So, um, now you see Docker isn't just a container runtime alone.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 31 | **Type:** Command
  - 
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 32 | **Type:** Concept
  - There was support for volumes of security.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 33 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - And finally also the container runtime called Runcie and the daemon that managed Runcie.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 34 | **Type:** Concept
  - And that's that was called as container.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 35 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So container D is CRI compatible and can work directly with Kubernetes as all other runtimes.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 36 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So container D can be used as a runtime on its own separate from Docker.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 37 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So now you have container D as a separate runtime and Docker separately.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 38 | **Type:** Concept
  - So Kubernetes continued to maintain support for Docker Engine directly.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 39 | **Type:** Concept
  - However having to maintain the Docker shim was an unnecessary effort and added complications, so it was decided in version 1.24 release of Kubernetes to remove Dockershim completely, and so support for Docker was removed.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 40 | **Type:** Concept
  - But you see all the images that were built, uh, before Docker was removed.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 41 | **Type:** Concept
  - So all the Docker images, uh, continue to work because Docker followed the image spec from the OCI standard.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 42 | **Type:** Concept
  - So all the images built by Docker follow the standard.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 43 | **Type:** Concept
  - So they continue to work with Containerd.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 44 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - But Docker itself was removed as a supported runtime from Kubernetes.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 45 | **Type:** Concept
  - So that's kind of the whole story.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 46 | **Type:** Concept
  - And now let's look into container D more specifically.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 47 | **Type:** Concept
  - So container D although is part of Docker, is a separate project on its own now and is a member of CNCF, uh, with the graduated uh status.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 48 | **Type:** Concept
  - So you can now install container D on its own without having to install Docker itself.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 49 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - So if you don't really need Docker other features, you could ideally just install container uh d alone.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 50 | **Type:** Concept
  - So typically we ran containers uh using the docker run command.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 51 | **Type:** Concept
  - Uh when we, when we had Docker.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 52 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - And if Docker isn't installed then how do you run containers with just uh, container D.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 53 | **Type:** Concept
  - Now once you install Containerd, it comes with a command line tool called Ktor.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 54 | **Type:** Troubleshooting
  - And this tool is solely made for debugging Containerd and is not very user friendly as it only supports a limited set of features.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 55 | **Type:** Concept
  - And this is what you can see in the documentation pages for for this particular tool.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 56 | **Type:** Concept
  - So for the other than the limited set of features that it provides, any any other way that you want to interact with Containerd, you'll have to rely on making API calls directly, which is not the the most user friendly way for us to operate.
- **File:** `008_Docker-vs-ContainerD.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 57 | **Type:** Concept

### A note on Docker deprecation

- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 1 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - Every time we mention about Docker in this course, one of the common questions we get is why are we still talking about Docker if it's deprecated?
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 2 | **Type:** Concept
  - And I realized that there's some confusion about the Docker deprecation among students, and I just wanted to take a minute to try and help clear that confusion.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 3 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So as we discussed before, Docker was the original and only supported container runtime for Kubernetes, and to make Kubernetes open to other runtimes, we had the container runtime interface introduced.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 4 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - So Docker consisted of multiple tools put together like Docker CLI, the API, the build tools that help build images.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 5 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - There was support for volumes, auth, security and finally also the container runtime called Runc and the daemon that managed the runtime called the container.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 6 | **Type:** Concept
  - So container D is the CRI compatible and can.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 7 | **Type:** Concept
  - And that's the component that can work directly with Kubernetes.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 8 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - And as all of the other runtimes.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 9 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - So container D can be used as runtime on its own separate from Docker.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 10 | **Type:** Concept
  - So once this change was made, Kubernetes no longer needed.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 11 | **Type:** Concept
  - The other tools that Docker supported like Docker CLI or the API, or build volumes or etc. as they were all taken care of of by Kubernetes itself.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 12 | **Type:** Concept
  - And so Kubernetes was able to deprecate the support for Docker.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 13 | **Type:** Concept
  - Now that doesn't mean that Docker is entirely gone.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 14 | **Type:** Concept
  - So Docker is still the most popular container solution out there and used by many in their day to day development and build processes.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 15 | **Type:** Operational Insight
  - It's just that Kubernetes no longer require Docker as the runtime now.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 16 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - So going forward in this course, every time we talk about containers, we use Docker as an example.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 17 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - And that's absolutely fine because sometimes we learn how things work in containers first before looking at how it is done in container orchestration world of Kubernetes.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 18 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - So and in those cases it is okay to use Docker as an example.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 19 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - And if you don't happen to have Docker on your machine or are only using container, then you can still work with the same examples by replacing the docker command with the node control command, or most of the time.
- **File:** `009_A note on Docker deprecation.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 20 | **Type:** Concept
  - So I just wanted to throw that out there before we proceed.

### ETCD For Beginners

- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 1 | **Type:** Architecture
  - This is a quick introduction to etcd for beginners.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 2 | **Type:** Architecture
  - If you already know etcd.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 3 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Feel free to skip and head over to the next video where we discuss etcd in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 4 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In this video, we discuss what etcd is, what a key value store is, and how is it different from traditional databases, and how to quickly get started with etcd and how to use the client tool to operate etcd?
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 5 | **Type:** Best Practice
  - Later in this course, we will cover high availability, where we discuss what it means to be a distributed system, how etcd works in a cluster mode, what raft protocol is, and what are the best practices around the number of nodes in a cluster.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 6 | **Type:** Architecture
  - So what is etcd?
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 7 | **Type:** Concept
  - It is a distributed, reliable key value store that is simple, secure and fast.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 8 | **Type:** Concept
  - So let's break it up.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 9 | **Type:** Concept
  - So what is a key value store?
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 10 | **Type:** Concept
  - Let's start with traditional databases.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 11 | **Type:** Concept
  - Traditionally databases have been in a tabular format.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 12 | **Type:** Concept
  - You must have heard about SQL or relational databases.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 13 | **Type:** Concept
  - They store data in the form of rows and columns.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 14 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - For example, here is a table that stores information regarding few individuals.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 15 | **Type:** Concept
  - The row represents each person and the column represents the type of information being stored.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 16 | **Type:** Concept
  - Now say we want to add additional details about these individuals.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 17 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - Say for example salary.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 18 | **Type:** Concept
  - So we add an additional column.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 19 | **Type:** Concept
  - Doing so impacts the entire table and all of the individuals in them.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 20 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - We then add salary details to this column.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 21 | **Type:** Concept
  - However not all of them are working, so these cells remain empty.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 22 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - We are then required to store grade information.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 23 | **Type:** Concept
  - So we add a new column and update the students with their respective grades.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 24 | **Type:** Concept
  - Again, only students have grades, so the corresponding fields for adults are empty.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 25 | **Type:** Concept
  - Every time a new information needs to be added, the entire table is affected and leads to a lot of empty cells.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 26 | **Type:** Concept
  - So relational databases that we just discussed have a strict schema, can perform complex queries using SQL delivers good performance however, is very rigid in terms of flexibility and is best for structured data.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 27 | **Type:** Concept
  - A document store.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 28 | **Type:** Concept
  - Stores information in the form of documents, so each individual gets a document, and all information about that individual is stored within that file.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 29 | **Type:** Concept
  - These files can be in any format or structure, and changes to one file does not affect the others.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 30 | **Type:** Concept
  - The working individuals can have their files with salary fields, and the students can have their pages with grades only.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 31 | **Type:** Concept
  - You can add additional details to any of these documents without having to update other similar documents.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 32 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - Document stores typically store data in a JSON format, so comparing relational databases to document store document stores typically don't need a schema defined can be limiting in terms of performing complex queries by joining different tables.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 33 | **Type:** Concept
  - Delivers good performance, is very flexible thanks to the document structure, and is best suited for semi-structured data, as we call it now.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 34 | **Type:** Concept
  - A third type of storage option is what we call a key value store.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 35 | **Type:** Concept
  - It's super simple.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 36 | **Type:** Concept
  - Stores a value against a key.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 37 | **Type:** Concept
  - So the key is name.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 38 | **Type:** Concept
  - The value is John.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 39 | **Type:** Concept
  - Another key is location.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 40 | **Type:** Concept
  - Value is New York, key is age.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 41 | **Type:** Concept
  - Value is 45.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 42 | **Type:** Concept
  - Key is salary.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 43 | **Type:** Concept
  - Value is 5000.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 44 | **Type:** Concept
  - And we can also store a bit more complex data.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 45 | **Type:** Concept
  - So the key could be user John Doe semicolon John Doe.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 46 | **Type:** Concept
  - So the key could be user semicolon John Doe.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 47 | **Type:** Concept
  - And the value could be a set of properties or an entire JSON document itself.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 48 | **Type:** Comparison
  - So how does a key value store compare to other storage models?
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 49 | **Type:** Concept
  - Key value store does not necessarily have a schema, does not support complex queries.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 50 | **Type:** Concept
  - But performance is super fast and is very flexible that you can store just about anything without breaking anything else or worrying about data structures, and so it's best suited for simple fast lookup.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 51 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Etcd is one such key value store that's distributed and reliable.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 52 | **Type:** Concept
  - We'll talk more about what distributed and reliable means later in this course.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 53 | **Type:** Architecture
  - So how do you install and get started with etcd?

  - We download the binary, extract it and run it.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 55 | **Type:** Concept
  - Well, you download the relevant binary for your operating system from GitHub releases page.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 56 | **Type:** Architecture
  - We extract it and run the etcd executable.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 57 | **Type:** Concept
  - As simple as that.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 58 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Now when you run etcd, it starts a service that listens on port 2379 by default.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 59 | **Type:** Concept
  - So that's your server.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 60 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Note that this is the simplest form of running etcd server.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 61 | **Type:** Concept
  - You would ideally run it as a system service or as a pod on a Kubernetes cluster.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 62 | **Type:** Architecture
  - You can then attach any clients to the etcd service to store and retrieve information.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 63 | **Type:** Architecture
  - A default client that comes with etcd is etcd control client or etcd.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 64 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The etcd cuddle is a command line client for etcd.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 65 | **Type:** Concept
  - You can use it to store and retrieve key value pairs to store a key and value pair.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 66 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Run the etcd cuddle.

  - Put key one command followed by the value value one.

  - This creates an entry in the database with the information to retrieve the stored data.

  - Run the get key command to view more options.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 70 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Run the etcd cuddle command without any arguments.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 71 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Now you might come across different versions of commands while exploring etcd and related articles online.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 72 | **Type:** Architecture
  - So it's important to understand the history of etcd releases.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 73 | **Type:** Architecture
  - So you know what changed when the first version of etcd version 0.1 was released in August 2013.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 74 | **Type:** Concept
  - The official stable version, version 2.0, was released in February 2015.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 75 | **Type:** Concept
  - This is when the raft consensus algorithm was redesigned and supported more than 1000 writes per second.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 76 | **Type:** Concept
  - We'll talk more about that later.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 77 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In January 2017, etcd released version three with a lot more optimizations and performance improvements.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 78 | **Type:** Concept
  - Now, what's important to note is the change between version two and three.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 79 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The API versions change so the etcd command changed as well.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 80 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The older API, which used etcd cuddle set and etcd cuddle get commands instead of etcd cuddle put and get commands.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 81 | **Type:** Concept
  - In V2, we used uh to delete values.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 82 | **Type:** Concept
  - In v3 we use delete and there was no support for transactions in v2, but v3 does support transactions later on.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 83 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In November 2018, etcd became a CNCF incubator project, meaning the Cloud Native Computing Foundation took ownership of governing and supporting the project, and more versions were released through to November 2020, when etcd became a CNCF graduat...
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 84 | **Type:** Concept
  - In June 2021, version 3.5 was released.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 85 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - So the point I'm trying to make is that you might see blogs documentation online regarding the older API, which used etcd cuddle set and get commands instead of the etcd cuddle put and get commands, so don't be alarmed.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 86 | **Type:** Concept
  - That's because they are on older version.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 87 | **Type:** Architecture
  - You can see the version by running the etcd cuddle version command, and if you look at the API version, you'll see whether you're on version 2 or 3.
- **File:** `010_ETCD For Beginners.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 88 | **Type:** Concept
  - The newer version uses put and get and delete commands instead of the set, get and rm commands.

### ETCD in Kubernetes

- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 1 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In the previous lecture, we discussed the basics of etcd.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 2 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In this lecture we will talk about etcd role in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 3 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The etcd data store stores information regarding the cluster such as the nodes, pods, configs, secrets, accounts, roles, role bindings and others.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 4 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Every information you see when you run the kubectl get command is from etcd server.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 5 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Every change you make to your cluster, such as adding additional nodes, deploying pods, or replica sets are updated in etcd server only once it is updated in etcd server.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 6 | **Type:** Concept
  - Is the change considered to be complete?
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 7 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Depending on how you set up your cluster, etcd is deployed differently.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 8 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - Throughout this section, we discuss about two types of Kubernetes deployments one deployed from scratch and other using the Kube ADM tool.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 9 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - The practice test environments are deployed using the cube ADM tool.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 10 | **Type:** Concept
  - And later in this course, when we set up a cluster, we set it up from scratch.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 11 | **Type:** Comparison
  - So it's good to know the difference between the two methods.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 12 | **Type:** Architecture
  - If you set up your cluster from scratch, then you deploy etcd by downloading the etcd binaries yourself, installing the binaries, and configuring etcd as a service in your master node yourself.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 13 | **Type:** Concept
  - There are many options passed into the service.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 14 | **Type:** Concept
  - A number of them relate to certificates.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 15 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - We will learn more about these certificates, how to create them and how to configure them later in this course.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 16 | **Type:** Concept
  - We have a whole section on TLS certificates.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 17 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The others are about configuring etcd as a cluster.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 18 | **Type:** Concept
  - We will look at those options when we set up high availability in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 19 | **Type:** Concept
  - The only option to note for now is the advertised client URL.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 20 | **Type:** Architecture
  - This is the address on which etcd listens.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 21 | **Type:** Architecture
  - It happens to be on the IP of the server and on port 2379, which is the default port on which etcd listens.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 22 | **Type:** Best Practice
  - This is the URL that should be configured on the kube API server when it tries to reach the etcd server.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 23 | **Type:** Architecture
  - If you set up your cluster using kube adm, then kube adm deploys the etcd server for you as a pod in the kube system namespace.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 24 | **Type:** Architecture
  - You can explore the etcd database using the etcd control utility within this pod.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 25 | **Type:** Architecture
  - To list all keys stored by Kubernetes, run the etcd control.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 26 | **Type:** Concept
  - Get command like this.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 27 | **Type:** Concept
  - Kubernetes stores data in a specific directory structure.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 28 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - The root directory is a registry, and under that you have the various Kubernetes constructs such as minions or nodes, pods, replica sets, deployments, etc. in a high availability environment, you will have multiple master nodes in your cluster.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 29 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - Then you will have multiple etcd instances spread across the master nodes.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 30 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In that case, make sure that the etcd instances know about each other by setting the right parameter in etcd service configuration.
- **File:** `011_ETCD in Kubernetes.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 31 | **Type:** Architecture

### Kube-API Server

- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 1 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In this lecture we will talk about the cube API server in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 2 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Earlier we discussed that the cube API server is the primary management component in Kubernetes.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 3 | **Type:** Architecture
  - When you run a cube control command, the cube control utility is in fact reaching to the cube API server.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 4 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The cube API server first authenticates the request and validates it.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 5 | **Type:** Architecture
  - It then retrieves the data from the etcd cluster and responds back with the requested information.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 6 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - You don't really need to use the cube control command line instead.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 7 | **Type:** Concept
  - You could also invoke the APIs directly by sending a Post request like this.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 8 | **Type:** Exam Tip
  - Let's look at an example of creating a pod.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 9 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - When you do that, as before, the request is authenticated first and then validated.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 10 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In this case, the API server creates a Pod object without assigning it to a node.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 11 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Updates the information in the etcd server.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 12 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - Updates the user that the pod has been created.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 13 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The scheduler continuously monitors the API server and realizes that there is a new pod with no node assigned.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 14 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The scheduler identifies the right node to place the new pod part on and communicates that back to the cube API server.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 15 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The API server then updates the information in the etcd cluster.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 16 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The API server then passes that information to the Kubelet in the appropriate worker node.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 17 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The Kubelet then creates the pod on the node and instructs the container runtime engine to deploy the application image.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 18 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Once done, the Kubelet updates the status back to the API server, and the API server then updates the data back in the etcd cluster.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 19 | **Type:** Concept
  - A similar pattern is followed every time a change is requested.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 20 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The kube API server is at the center of all the different tasks that needs to be performed to make a change in the cluster.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 21 | **Type:** Architecture
  - To summarize, the kube API server is responsible for authenticating and validating requests, retrieving and updating data in the etcd data store.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 22 | **Type:** Architecture
  - In fact, kube API server is the only component that interacts directly with the etcd data store.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 23 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The other components, such as the scheduler, kube, controller, manager, and Kubelet uses the API server to perform updates in the cluster in their respective areas.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 24 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - If you bootstrapped your cluster using kube admin tool, Then you don't need to know this, but if you are setting up the hard way, then the cube API server is available as a binary in the Kubernetes release page.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 25 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - Download it and configure it to run as a service on your Kubernetes master node.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 26 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The cube API server is run with a lot of parameters, as you can see here.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 27 | **Type:** Architecture
  - Throughout this section, we're going to take a peek at how to install and configure these individual components of the Kubernetes architecture.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 28 | **Type:** Warning/Pitfall
  - You don't have to understand all of the options right now, but I think having a high level understanding on some of these now will make it easier later when we configure the whole cluster and all of its components from scratch.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 29 | **Type:** Architecture
  - The Kubernetes architecture consists of a lot of different components working with each other, talking to each other in many different ways.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 30 | **Type:** Concept
  - So they all need to know where the other components are.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 31 | **Type:** Implementation Step
  - There are different modes of authentication, authorization, encryption, and security, and that's why you have so many options.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 32 | **Type:** Concept
  - When we go through the relevant section in the course, we will pull up this file and look at the relevant options.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 33 | **Type:** Concept
  - For now, we will look at a few important ones.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 34 | **Type:** Concept
  - A lot of them are certificates that are used to secure the connectivity between different components.

  - We look at these certificates in more detail when we go through the SSL TLS certificates lecture later in this course.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 36 | **Type:** Concept
  - There is a whole section just for it, so we will get rid of them for now.

  - The option etcd servers is where you specify the location of the etcd servers.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 39 | **Type:** Architecture
  - This is how the kube API server connects to the etcd servers.
- **File:** `013_Kube-API Server.extraction.md` | **Entry:** 40 | **Type:** Architecture
  - So how do you view the kube API server options in an existing cluster?
